Yasmeen1|<<This middle-aged woman looks worn down to the bone, with bags under her eyes and deep worry lines in her forehead. Her jet-black hair is unkempt but held in place by a long, ornamented pin of surprising finery.>>||||
Yasmeen2|Oh, hello. Are you one of [[Nadja's]] pals? I'm afraid she's not seeing anyone right now.||||
Yasmeen3|<<A cloud crosses her face.>> ((Vidal?)) The vision trader? Of all the ((nerve)) – !||||
Yasmeen4|<<Something about your manner seems to cut her, and when she speaks her voice cracks as if she's about to cry.>> ##I... no. No, she's ((not)) all right.||||
Yasmeen5|<<The woman closes her eyes and takes a deep breath.>> ##I apologise, stranger. You're... not seeing me at my best just now.||||
Yasmeen6|<<She makes a small noise of polite amusement.>> ##This tenement is a maze, isn't it? If there's any order to the room numbers, I've never mastered it.||||
Yasmeen7|Well, stranger, I hope you find what you're looking for.||||
Yasmeen8|I'm Nadja's mother, [[Yasmeen]]. This last month I've been her full-time carer as well. ##It's those [[bottled visions]], you see.||||
Yasmeen9|Our family has had a rough few years, and there wasn't much joy in our lives. So when Nadja first started getting into visions, I was happy for her.||||
Yasmeen10|Then she began spending all her free time dreaming. Soon she was sleeping until noon, missing work. ##Now she [[barely wakes up at all]], and she's never lucid when she does.||||
Yasmeen11|She can't work; can't even feed herself. But she ((does)) need food, and fuel to keep warm. With all these summoning glitches I have to pay cash on the black market, and we're down to the last dregs of our savings.||||
Yasmeen12|<<Yasmeen shrugs despairingly.>> ##I just don't know how we can ((survive)) like this for much longer.||||
Yasmeen13|A few years ago my husband passed away, and I got very sick. The Creeping Cough, you know. Even today I can't really work, because of all the spores in my lungs.||||
Yasmeen14|Then, last year, we had to leave [[our house]] in the countryside due to the Corruption. As far as I know it's still out there, slowly sinking back into the mud. This room and its contents are all we have left.||||
Yasmeen15|I don't mean to moan, truly. There's so many in this kingdom who have it worse than us. I just know it was tough on Nadja, that's all.||||
Yasmeen16|<<Yasmeen throws up her hands in frustration.>> I don't know! I'm not an alchemist, or any kind of vision expert. We petitioned the King for a doctor to visit, but with the way things are it'll be ((months)) before we hear back.||||
Yasmeen17|<<A tentative hope is kindled in her eyes.>> Oh, would you? ##Yes, you could ask [[Vidal the vision trader]] about it. I doubt I could face him myself without knocking his lights out and trashing his shop...||||

Yasmeen20|Thank you, dear. ##But, um, could I ask you a favour? I'll understand if it's not possible, of course...||||
Yasmeen21|Should you happen to find yourself in [[Vidal's bottled vision shop]], perhaps you could ask him about Nadja? If there's any way to help her, he'd surely know.||||
Yasmeen22|<<You find Yasmeen feeding her daughter porridge from a wooden bowl, singing a soft lullaby. She looks worn down to the bone.>>||||
Yasmeen23|<<Yasmeen glances in your direction.>> ##Ah, hello again. Did you have any luck?||||

Yasmeen29|It's not far from here. Just opposite the Machinarium, beside the steps that lead up from the lower city.||||

Yasmeen44b|<<She sighs.>> What I wouldn't do to taste his fish goulash again! Or to hear Bina sing again...||||

Yasmeen49|Yes. In theory it's the obvious choice. I don't know how to care for Nadja properly, let alone bottle her visions. But ((they)) do. And obviously, the money wouldn't go amiss.||||
Yasmeen50|<<She pats the contract you gave her.>> If the figures described here are even halfway accurate, I'd be able to live comfortably for as long as Nadja's illness lasts.||||
Yasmeen51|Yes. You can't put a price on family. I may not know how to care for Nadja properly, or bottle visions. But I can learn. King knows I've seen a lot of change in my life.||||
Yasmeen52|Although... it ((would)) be a lot of work. If my sickness flares up, I might not be able to keep the business going. We could easily end up back where we started, without a penny.||||
Yasmeen53|My heart tells me I should keep Nadja here. No matter how long it takes for me to learn the vision trade, or how difficult it would be to take care of her.||||
Yasmeen54|And if there's ((any)) way that I can still communicate with her – even if it's only through dreams – I want to take it.||||
